## Chapter: Chapter 12: Waste Management and Recycling:

### Introduction

The city of Cartagena, like many other urban centers in the Global South, faces a unique set of challenges when it comes to waste management and recycling. This chapter will delve into these challenges, exploring the complex interplay between urbanization, economic development, and waste generation. 

As we have seen in previous chapters, urbanization and economic development often go hand in hand, leading to increased waste generation. However, the capacity of waste management systems in many cities in the Global South is often insufficient to handle this increased waste. This results in inadequate waste collection, poor disposal practices, and a significant amount of waste ending up in the environment. 

Moreover, the chapter will also explore the opportunities for waste reduction and recycling in Cartagena. It will discuss the potential for waste reduction through source separation and recycling, and the role of technology and innovation in waste management. 

The chapter will also highlight the importance of policy and governance in waste management and recycling. It will discuss the need for effective waste management policies and regulations, and the role of governance structures in ensuring the implementation of these policies. 

In conclusion, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of the challenges and opportunities for waste management and recycling in Cartagena. It will serve as a guide for policymakers, urban planners, and waste management professionals in the city, and provide valuable insights for other cities facing similar challenges in the Global South.




#### 11.3b Role of Nutrition Policies in Food Security

Nutrition policies play a pivotal role in addressing food security in the Global South. Food security is a complex issue that encompasses the availability, access, and utilization of food. Nutrition policies aim to improve these aspects by promoting healthy food choices, addressing food insecurity, and improving nutrition education.

##### 11.3b.1 Nutrition Policies and Food Availability

Nutrition policies can influence food availability by promoting the production and distribution of nutrient-rich foods. This can be achieved through policies that support sustainable agriculture practices, reduce food waste, and promote local food production. For instance, the Sustainable Development Goal 12.3 aims to halve food waste by 2030, which can increase food availability and reduce food insecurity.

##### 11.3b.2 Nutrition Policies and Food Access

Nutrition policies can also improve food access by promoting equitable distribution of food. This can be achieved through policies that address the root causes of food insecurity, such as poverty, social inequality, and conflict. For example, the 2015-2020 Dietary Guidelines for Americans emphasize the importance of addressing food insecurity and promoting equitable access to healthy food options.

##### 11.3b.3 Nutrition Policies and Food Utilization

Nutrition policies can improve food utilization by promoting healthy eating habits and nutrition education. This can be achieved through policies that support the development and implementation of dietary guidelines, such as MyPlate, and promote nutrition education in schools and communities. For instance, the 2015-2020 Dietary Guidelines for Americans include recommendations for healthy eating patterns that can improve food utilization and reduce the risk of diet-related diseases.

In conclusion, nutrition policies play a crucial role in addressing food security in the Global South. By promoting healthy food choices, addressing food insecurity, and improving nutrition education, these policies can contribute to a more food-secure future for all.

#### 11.3c Case Studies of Nutrition Policies in Food Security

In this section, we will explore some case studies that highlight the role of nutrition policies in food security. These case studies will provide real-world examples of how nutrition policies can be implemented and their impact on food security.

##### 11.3c.1 The Role of Nutrition Policies in Food Security in Brazil

Brazil has made significant strides in improving food security through its nutrition policies. The Brazilian government has implemented a comprehensive set of policies aimed at improving food security, including the Bolsa Familia program, which provides cash transfers to poor families, and the Escola de Criana program, which provides free meals to children in public schools. These policies have helped to reduce food insecurity in Brazil, with the number of undernourished people falling from 16.5 million in 2003 to 7.5 million in 2013[^1^].

##### 11.3c.2 The Role of Nutrition Policies in Food Security in India

In India, the National Food Security Act (NFSA) has been instrumental in improving food security. The NFSA provides for the right to food for all Indians, with a focus on vulnerable groups such as children, pregnant women, and lactating mothers. The act also mandates the provision of subsidized food grains to these groups. However, despite these efforts, food insecurity remains a significant issue in India, with an estimated 194 million people still undernourished[^2^]. This highlights the need for a more comprehensive approach to food security, including addressing the root causes of food insecurity.

##### 11.3c.3 The Role of Nutrition Policies in Food Security in the United States

In the United States, the 2015-2020 Dietary Guidelines for Americans have been instrumental in promoting healthy eating habits and addressing food insecurity. The guidelines emphasize the importance of a healthy diet for all Americans, including those with limited resources. They also provide recommendations for healthy eating patterns that can help to improve food security. However, despite these efforts, food insecurity remains a significant issue in the United States, with an estimated 37 million people, including 11 million children, facing food insecurity[^3^]. This highlights the need for a more comprehensive approach to food security in the United States, including addressing the root causes of food insecurity.

These case studies highlight the importance of nutrition policies in addressing food security. They also underscore the need for a comprehensive approach to food security, including addressing the root causes of food insecurity.

[^1^]: FAO. (2015). The State of Food and Agriculture 2015. Rome.
[^2^]: FAO. (2017). The State of Food and Agriculture 2017. Rome.
[^3^]: USDA. (2015). 2015-2020 Dietary Guidelines for Americans. Washington, D.C.




#### 11.3c Case Studies of Successful Nutrition Policies

In this section, we will explore some case studies of successful nutrition policies in the Global South. These examples will provide practical insights into how nutrition policies can be effectively implemented to address food security and nutrition challenges.

##### 11.3c.1 Case Study 1: Brazil's Zero Hunger Program

Brazil's Zero Hunger Program, launched in 2003, is a prime example of a successful nutrition policy in the Global South. The program aims to eradicate hunger and malnutrition in the country, and it has made significant strides in improving food security and nutrition.

The program's key strategies include:

- Expansion of school feeding programs: The program has significantly expanded the school feeding program, ensuring that over 40 million children receive a daily meal at school. This has not only improved food availability but also increased school attendance and improved learning outcomes.

- Promotion of family agriculture: The program has supported small-scale farmers, particularly women, to increase their productivity and income. This has not only improved food availability but also empowered women and reduced poverty.

- Implementation of food and nutrition surveillance: The program has implemented a comprehensive food and nutrition surveillance system to monitor food security and nutrition at the national and local levels. This has enabled policymakers to make evidence-based decisions and target interventions effectively.

##### 11.3c.2 Case Study 2: India's Mid-Day Meal Scheme

India's Mid-Day Meal Scheme, launched in 1995, is another successful example of a nutrition policy in the Global South. The scheme aims to provide a hot cooked meal to all children in government and government-aided schools.

The scheme's key strategies include:

- Universal coverage: The scheme provides a meal to all children in government and government-aided schools, regardless of their socio-economic status. This has improved food access and reduced food insecurity among school-going children.

- Local procurement: The scheme promotes local procurement of food, which not only improves food availability but also supports local economies.

- Nutritional standards: The scheme has established nutritional standards for the meal, ensuring that children receive a balanced and nutritious meal. This has improved food utilization and reduced the risk of diet-related diseases.

These case studies demonstrate that with careful planning and implementation, nutrition policies can be effective in addressing food security and nutrition challenges in the Global South. They highlight the importance of considering the local context, involving all stakeholders, and monitoring and evaluating the policy's impact.

This requires collaboration and coordination among all stakeholders, as well as a commitment to long-term solutions.

Another important aspect to consider is the role of technology and innovation in addressing food security and nutrition. As we have seen in previous chapters, there are many innovative solutions being implemented in Cartagena, such as urban agriculture and food waste reduction initiatives. These solutions not only have the potential to improve food security and nutrition, but also to create jobs and stimulate the local economy.

In conclusion, addressing food security and nutrition in Cartagena is a complex and challenging task, but it is also a crucial one. By taking a multi-faceted approach and leveraging technology and innovation, we can work towards creating a more food secure and nutritious future for the city and its residents.

### Subsection: 12.1a Basics of Poverty

Poverty is a complex issue that affects millions of people around the world, particularly in the Global South. It is a state of being without sufficient access to the goods, services, and opportunities necessary for a decent standard of living. In this section, we will explore the basics of poverty, including its definition, causes, and impacts.

#### 12.1a.1 Definition of Poverty

Poverty is a multidimensional concept that encompasses more than just income levels. It is a complex social, economic, and political condition characterized by a lack of basic human needs, opportunities, and choices. The United Nations defines poverty as "a state of extreme social, economic and political exclusion of individuals, groups and communities, as well as a violation of their human rights." This definition highlights the multifaceted nature of poverty and emphasizes the importance of addressing not just material deprivation, but also social and political exclusion.

#### 12.1a.2 Causes of Poverty

Poverty is caused by a variety of factors, both structural and individual. Structural causes of poverty include unequal power dynamics, discrimination, and systemic barriers to opportunity. For example, in the United States, Rank, Yoon, and Hirschl (2003) argue that poverty is a result of "failings at the structural level," including a saturated labor market that offers low-paying, part-time jobs with no benefits. This structural failure contributes to the inability of many families to earn enough to keep them above the poverty line.

Individual causes of poverty include personal choices and behaviors, such as substance abuse, criminal activity, and poor decision-making. However, these individual factors are often influenced by structural factors, such as limited educational opportunities and economic disparities. For instance, a person may choose to engage in criminal activity due to limited job opportunities and the allure of quick money.

#### 12.1a.3 Impacts of Poverty

Poverty has far-reaching impacts on individuals, families, and communities. It is associated with a range of negative outcomes, including poor health, low educational attainment, and increased risk of social exclusion and discrimination. Poverty also has significant implications for food security, as it limits access to nutritious food and increases the risk of food insecurity.

In the next section, we will delve deeper into the relationship between poverty and food security, exploring the challenges and opportunities for addressing food insecurity in the context of poverty.




#### 12.1b Role of Poverty in Food Security

Poverty plays a significant role in food security, particularly in the Global South. Food security is defined by the United Nations as the condition in which all people, at all times, have physical, social, and economic access to sufficient, safe, and nutritious food. Poverty, on the other hand, is a state of being without sufficient access to the goods, services, and opportunities necessary for a decent standard of living. Therefore, poverty is a key determinant of food security.

#### 12.1b.1 Poverty and Hunger

Hunger is a direct consequence of poverty. According to the World Health Organization, hunger is a major public health issue that affects 690 million people worldwide. The majority of these people live in developing countries, where poverty is a significant factor contributing to hunger. Poverty limits people's ability to access food, as it often means they cannot afford to buy enough food to meet their nutritional needs. This is particularly true in urban areas, where the cost of living is often higher and the competition for resources is greater.

#### 12.1b.2 Poverty and Nutrition

Poverty also has a significant impact on nutrition. Malnutrition, which is a result of inadequate nutrition, is a major health issue among the poor. According to the World Health Organization, malnutrition is a key factor in the deaths of nearly 3 million children under the age of five each year. Poverty limits people's ability to access a diverse and nutritious diet, which is essential for good health. This is particularly true for women and children, who are often the most vulnerable members of a household.

#### 12.1b.3 Poverty and Agriculture

Poverty also affects agriculture, which is a key source of food and income for many people in the Global South. Poverty often means that small-scale farmers, who make up the majority of the rural poor, lack access to the necessary resources and technologies to increase their agricultural productivity. This limits their ability to grow enough food to meet their own needs, let alone to sell surplus produce for income. As a result, these farmers and their families often go hungry.

In conclusion, poverty plays a crucial role in food security. Addressing poverty is therefore a key step towards achieving food security in the Global South. This requires a multifaceted approach that includes improving agricultural productivity, increasing access to food, and addressing the social and economic exclusion that often accompanies poverty.

#### 12.1c Strategies to Reduce Poverty

Reducing poverty is a complex task that requires a multifaceted approach. In this section, we will explore some strategies that can be used to reduce poverty, particularly in the context of food security.

##### 12.1c.1 Improving Agricultural Productivity

As we have seen, poverty often limits people's ability to access a diverse and nutritious diet. This is particularly true for small-scale farmers in the Global South, who often lack access to the necessary resources and technologies to increase their agricultural productivity. Improving agricultural productivity can therefore be an effective strategy for reducing poverty and improving food security.

This can be achieved through various means, including:

- Increasing access to pro-poor technologies: As mentioned in the related context, improvements in agricultural productivity aimed at small-scale farmers will benefit the rural poor first. This can be achieved by increasing access to pro-poor technologies, which are designed to meet the specific needs and constraints of poor farmers.

- Investing in irrigation: According to the Comprehensive Assessment of Water Management in Agriculture, managing rainwater and soil moisture more effectively, and using supplemental and small-scale irrigation, hold the key to helping the greatest number of poor people. This can be achieved through targeted investments in irrigation infrastructure.

- Expanding cropped areas: Increasing the area under cultivation can also increase agricultural productivity. This can be achieved by providing poor farmers with access to land and resources.

##### 12.1c.2 Increasing Access to Food

In addition to improving agricultural productivity, increasing access to food is another key strategy for reducing poverty. This can be achieved through various means, including:

- Implementing food safety net programs: Food safety net programs, such as food stamps or food vouchers, can provide poor households with access to food. These programs can be particularly effective in urban areas, where the cost of living is often higher and the competition for resources is greater.

- Promoting social protection: Social protection measures, such as cash transfers or public works programs, can provide poor households with a regular income, which can be used to purchase food. These measures can also help to reduce the vulnerability of poor households to shocks, such as illness or natural disasters.

##### 12.1c.3 Addressing Social and Economic Exclusion

Finally, reducing poverty also requires addressing the social and economic exclusion that often accompanies poverty. This can be achieved by promoting social inclusion, which involves ensuring that poor people have equal access to resources, opportunities, and services. This can be achieved through various means, including:

- Promoting inclusive education: Education is a key tool for reducing poverty. However, poor children often face barriers to education, such as lack of access to schools or resources. Promoting inclusive education can help to ensure that all children, regardless of their socio-economic status, have equal access to education.

- Promoting inclusive employment: Poor people often face barriers to employment, such as lack of skills or discrimination. Promoting inclusive employment can help to ensure that poor people have equal opportunities to participate in the labor market.

In conclusion, reducing poverty is a complex task that requires a multifaceted approach. By improving agricultural productivity, increasing access to food, and addressing social and economic exclusion, we can work towards reducing poverty and improving food security in the Global South.




#### 12.1c Case Studies of Poverty and Food Security

To further understand the impact of poverty on food security, let's examine some case studies from the Global South.

#### 12.1c.1 Poverty and Food Security in Cartagena, Colombia

Cartagena, a major port city in Colombia, has a population of over 1.2 million people. The city is home to a diverse population, with a significant number of poor and vulnerable populations. According to the World Bank, over 30% of the population lives in poverty, with over 10% living in extreme poverty.

The city's food security is heavily dependent on its agricultural sector, which is primarily focused on the production of bananas, coffee, and shrimp. However, the city's food security is threatened by various factors, including climate change, economic instability, and social inequality.

Climate change has led to changes in weather patterns, resulting in more frequent and severe droughts and floods. These events have a direct impact on the city's agricultural sector, leading to food shortages and price increases. Economic instability, due to factors such as the global economic crisis and the Colombian conflict, has also contributed to food insecurity in the city. The high cost of living and the limited access to affordable food options have made it difficult for the city's poor and vulnerable populations to access adequate food.

#### 12.1c.2 Poverty and Food Security in Nairobi, Kenya

Nairobi, the capital of Kenya, is home to over 4 million people. The city has a diverse population, with a significant number of poor and vulnerable populations. According to the World Bank, over 40% of the population lives in poverty, with over 20% living in extreme poverty.

The city's food security is heavily dependent on its agricultural sector, which is primarily focused on the production of maize, beans, and milk. However, the city's food security is threatened by various factors, including climate change, economic instability, and social inequality.

Climate change has led to changes in weather patterns, resulting in more frequent and severe droughts and floods. These events have a direct impact on the city's agricultural sector, leading to food shortages and price increases. Economic instability, due to factors such as the global economic crisis and the Kenyan conflict, has also contributed to food insecurity in the city. The high cost of living and the limited access to affordable food options have made it difficult for the city's poor and vulnerable populations to access adequate food.

#### 12.1c.3 Poverty and Food Security in Dhaka, Bangladesh

Dhaka, the capital of Bangladesh, is home to over 18 million people. The city has a diverse population, with a significant number of poor and vulnerable populations. According to the World Bank, over 50% of the population lives in poverty, with over 25% living in extreme poverty.

The city's food security is heavily dependent on its agricultural sector, which is primarily focused on the production of rice, vegetables, and fish. However, the city's food security is threatened by various factors, including climate change, economic instability, and social inequality.

Climate change has led to changes in weather patterns, resulting in more frequent and severe floods and droughts. These events have a direct impact on the city's agricultural sector, leading to food shortages and price increases. Economic instability, due to factors such as the global economic crisis and the Bangladeshi conflict, has also contributed to food insecurity in the city. The high cost of living and the limited access to affordable food options have made it difficult for the city's poor and vulnerable populations to access adequate food.




#### 12.2a Understanding Poverty Reduction Strategies

Poverty reduction strategies are comprehensive plans developed by governments and international organizations to address the root causes of poverty and promote sustainable development. These strategies are designed to address the complex interplay between poverty, food security, and other social, economic, and environmental factors. They aim to create an enabling environment for poverty reduction by promoting economic growth, social inclusion, and good governance.

Poverty reduction strategies are typically developed through a participatory process that involves the active participation of the poor and vulnerable populations. This ensures that the strategies are responsive to the needs and aspirations of the people and promotes community ownership. The strategies are then implemented through a range of interventions, including policy reforms, public expenditures, and community-based programs.

The effectiveness of poverty reduction strategies is often evaluated based on their impact on poverty, food security, and other development outcomes. This involves monitoring and assessing the progress made towards the strategy's objectives and identifying areas for improvement. Lessons learned from these evaluations are used to inform the development of future strategies and policies.

#### 12.2b Poverty Reduction Strategies and Food Security

Food security is a key component of poverty reduction strategies. It is defined as the condition in which all people, at all times, have physical, social, and economic access to sufficient, safe, and nutritious food. Poverty reduction strategies aim to improve food security by addressing the underlying causes of food insecurity, including poverty, lack of access to productive resources, and vulnerability to shocks and stresses.

Poverty reduction strategies also aim to promote sustainable food systems that are resilient to shocks and stresses. This involves promoting sustainable agricultural practices, diversifying food production systems, and improving market access for small-scale producers. It also involves strengthening social protection systems to ensure that the poor and vulnerable populations have access to adequate food and nutrition.

#### 12.2c Case Studies of Poverty Reduction Strategies

To further understand the role of poverty reduction strategies in promoting food security, let's examine some case studies from the Global South.

##### 12.2c.1 Poverty Reduction Strategy in Honduras

In 1999, 66 percent of Hondurans were poor. The government, with the support of international organizations, developed a Poverty Reduction Strategy (PRS) to address the root causes of poverty. The strategy was developed through a participatory process that involved the active participation of the poor and vulnerable populations. It covered a range of areas, including education and literacy, diet and nutrition, and access to potable water. The strategy was implemented through a range of interventions, including policy reforms, public expenditures, and community-based programs.

The PRS has been effective in reducing poverty and improving food security in Honduras. By 2015, the poverty rate had been reduced from 66 percent to 40 percent. The strategy has also improved food security by promoting sustainable food systems and strengthening social protection systems. However, there are still challenges to be addressed, including the need for more effective policy implementation and the need to address the root causes of poverty and inequality.

##### 12.2c.2 Poverty Reduction Strategy in Cartagena, Colombia

In Cartagena, Colombia, the government has implemented a poverty reduction strategy to address the high levels of poverty and food insecurity in the city. The strategy aims to improve food security by promoting sustainable food systems and strengthening social protection systems. It also aims to address the root causes of poverty, including economic instability, social inequality, and climate change.

The strategy has been effective in improving food security in Cartagena. The city's food security has been strengthened through the promotion of sustainable agricultural practices, the diversification of food production systems, and the improvement of market access for small-scale producers. The strategy has also strengthened social protection systems to ensure that the poor and vulnerable populations have access to adequate food and nutrition. However, there are still challenges to be addressed, including the need for more effective policy implementation and the need to address the root causes of poverty and inequality.

#### 12.2d Challenges and Opportunities for Action in Poverty Reduction Strategies

Despite the successes achieved in poverty reduction strategies, there are still significant challenges to be addressed. These challenges include the need for more effective policy implementation, the need to address the root causes of poverty and inequality, and the need to ensure the sustainability of poverty reduction efforts.

There are also opportunities for action in poverty reduction strategies. These opportunities include the potential for technology and innovation to improve the effectiveness of poverty reduction efforts, the potential for partnerships and collaboration to scale up successful interventions, and the potential for learning and adaptation to improve the design and implementation of poverty reduction strategies.

In conclusion, poverty reduction strategies play a crucial role in promoting food security and sustainable development in the Global South. They provide a comprehensive framework for addressing the root causes of poverty and promoting sustainable development. However, there is still much work to be done to ensure the effectiveness and sustainability of these strategies.

#### 12.2d.1 Challenges in Poverty Reduction Strategies

One of the main challenges in poverty reduction strategies is the need for more effective policy implementation. Despite the development of comprehensive strategies, many of these strategies are not fully implemented due to a lack of resources, capacity, and political will. This limits their effectiveness in reducing poverty and improving food security.

Another challenge is the need to address the root causes of poverty and inequality. Poverty reduction strategies often focus on addressing the symptoms of poverty, such as food insecurity, rather than the underlying causes. This can limit their effectiveness in reducing poverty in the long term.

Finally, there is a need to ensure the sustainability of poverty reduction efforts. Many strategies are funded by external donors, which can limit their sustainability. There is a need to develop strategies that are financially sustainable and can be implemented without external support.

#### 12.2d.2 Opportunities in Poverty Reduction Strategies

Despite these challenges, there are also opportunities for action in poverty reduction strategies. One of these opportunities is the potential for technology and innovation to improve the effectiveness of poverty reduction efforts. For example, the use of mobile technology can be used to improve the delivery of social protection programs and promote financial inclusion.

Partnerships and collaboration also present opportunities for scaling up successful interventions. By working together, different stakeholders can share resources, knowledge, and expertise to implement poverty reduction strategies on a larger scale.

Finally, there is an opportunity for learning and adaptation in poverty reduction strategies. By evaluating and learning from past experiences, strategies can be improved and adapted to better address the needs and challenges of different contexts.

In conclusion, poverty reduction strategies are crucial for promoting food security and sustainable development in the Global South. While there are challenges to be addressed, there are also opportunities for action that can help improve the effectiveness and sustainability of these strategies.

#### 12.2e Case Studies of Poverty Reduction Strategies

To further understand the challenges and opportunities in poverty reduction strategies, let's examine some case studies from the Global South.

##### 12.2e.1 Poverty Reduction Strategy in Honduras

In Honduras, the Poverty Reduction Strategy (PRS) was implemented in 2001 with the goal of reducing the poverty rate from 70% to 40% by 2015. The strategy was developed through a participatory process that involved the active participation of the poor and vulnerable populations. It covered a range of areas, including education and literacy, diet and nutrition, and access to potable water.

Despite the efforts, the PRS faced several challenges. The strategy was not fully implemented due to a lack of resources and capacity. Additionally, the root causes of poverty, such as economic instability and social inequality, were not adequately addressed. This limited the effectiveness of the strategy in reducing poverty in the long term.

However, there were also opportunities for action. The PRS provided an opportunity for learning and adaptation. The strategy was evaluated and adjusted over time, leading to improvements in its effectiveness. Additionally, the strategy was implemented in a context of economic growth, which contributed to a reduction in the poverty rate.

##### 12.2e.2 Poverty Reduction Strategy in Cartagena, Colombia

In Cartagena, Colombia, a poverty reduction strategy was implemented in 2003 with the goal of reducing the poverty rate from 40% to 20% by 2015. The strategy was developed through a participatory process that involved the active participation of the poor and vulnerable populations. It covered a range of areas, including education and literacy, diet and nutrition, and access to potable water.

Similar to the PRS in Honduras, the strategy faced challenges in terms of implementation and addressing the root causes of poverty. However, there were also opportunities for action. The strategy provided an opportunity for technology and innovation, as mobile technology was used to improve the delivery of social protection programs. Additionally, partnerships and collaboration were used to scale up successful interventions, leading to a reduction in the poverty rate.

These case studies highlight the importance of addressing the challenges and leveraging the opportunities in poverty reduction strategies. They also underscore the need for a comprehensive and participatory approach to poverty reduction, as well as the importance of learning and adaptation in improving the effectiveness of these strategies.




#### 12.2b Role of Poverty Reduction in Food Security

Poverty reduction plays a crucial role in improving food security in the Global South. As mentioned earlier, poverty is a major factor contributing to food insecurity. Therefore, addressing poverty is essential for ensuring food security. Poverty reduction strategies, when effectively implemented, can contribute to improving food security in several ways.

Firstly, poverty reduction strategies aim to increase the incomes of the poor. This is achieved through various means, including policy reforms, public expenditures, and community-based programs. Increased incomes enable the poor to access more food, thereby improving their food security. This is particularly important in the Global South, where a large proportion of the population lives in poverty and is therefore food insecure.

Secondly, poverty reduction strategies aim to improve the livelihoods of the poor. This involves providing them with access to productive resources, such as land, capital, and technology. Improved livelihoods can enhance the poor's ability to produce and access food, thereby improving their food security. This is particularly important in the Global South, where many of the poor are small-scale farmers who rely on agriculture for their livelihoods.

Thirdly, poverty reduction strategies aim to promote social inclusion. This involves ensuring that the poor have equal access to basic services, such as education, health, and social protection. Improved access to these services can enhance the poor's ability to cope with shocks and stresses, thereby improving their food security. This is particularly important in the Global South, where many of the poor are marginalized and excluded from society.

Finally, poverty reduction strategies aim to promote good governance. This involves ensuring that the poor have a voice in decision-making processes and that their rights are respected. Improved governance can enhance the poor's ability to access resources and services, thereby improving their food security. This is particularly important in the Global South, where many of the poor face significant barriers to accessing resources and services due to corruption, lack of transparency, and other governance issues.

In conclusion, poverty reduction plays a crucial role in improving food security in the Global South. By addressing the root causes of poverty and promoting sustainable development, poverty reduction strategies can contribute to creating an enabling environment for food security. However, it is important to note that poverty reduction is not a panacea for food security. Other factors, such as climate change, conflict, and economic instability, also play a significant role in food security and need to be addressed.

#### 12.2c Case Studies of Poverty Reduction and Food Security

To further illustrate the role of poverty reduction in food security, let's examine some case studies from the Global South. These case studies will provide concrete examples of how poverty reduction strategies have been implemented and their impact on food security.

##### Case Study 1: Brazil's Zero Hunger Program

Brazil's Zero Hunger Program, launched in 2003, is a prime example of a successful poverty reduction strategy that has also improved food security. The program aimed to reduce extreme poverty and hunger by providing direct food aid to the poor, as well as implementing policies to increase the incomes of the poor and improve their livelihoods.

The program's direct food aid component, known as the "Basic Food Basket," provided a monthly supply of staple foods to households with extreme poverty. This helped to ensure that these households had access to adequate food. Additionally, the program implemented policies to increase the incomes of the poor, such as increasing minimum wages and providing conditional cash transfers to poor households.

The program also aimed to improve the livelihoods of the poor by providing them with access to productive resources, such as land and credit. This helped to enhance the poor's ability to produce and access food. Furthermore, the program promoted social inclusion by ensuring that the poor had access to basic services, such as education and health care.

The impact of the Zero Hunger Program on food security in Brazil has been significant. According to the Food and Agriculture Organization (FAO), the prevalence of hunger in Brazil declined from 14.3% in 2003 to 8.5% in 2013. This represents a 39% reduction in hunger over this period.

##### Case Study 2: India's National Rural Employment Guarantee Scheme

India's National Rural Employment Guarantee Scheme (NREGS) is another example of a successful poverty reduction strategy that has improved food security. Launched in 2005, the NREGS aims to provide employment to rural households, particularly those in the poorest districts, for at least 100 days per year.

The NREGS provides a wage guarantee of 100 rupees per day, which is significantly higher than the minimum wage in many rural areas. This helps to increase the incomes of the poor and improve their livelihoods. Additionally, the NREGS aims to create assets, such as irrigation canals and roads, which can enhance the poor's ability to produce and access food.

The impact of the NREGS on food security in India has been significant. According to the World Bank, the NREGS has helped to reduce poverty in India by 10 percentage points between 2005 and 2011. This represents a 15% reduction in poverty over this period. Furthermore, the NREGS has helped to improve food security by increasing the incomes of the poor and enhancing their ability to produce and access food.

These case studies demonstrate the potential of poverty reduction strategies to improve food security in the Global South. By addressing the root causes of poverty and promoting sustainable development, these strategies can help to create an enabling environment for food security. However, it is important to note that these strategies must be implemented in a way that is responsive to the specific needs and circumstances of each country and community.




#### 12.2c Case Studies of Successful Poverty Reduction Strategies

In this section, we will explore some case studies of successful poverty reduction strategies in the Global South. These case studies will provide practical examples of how poverty reduction strategies can be implemented and the impact they can have on food security.

##### Case Study 1: Poverty Reduction Strategy in Honduras

Honduras is a country in Central America that has implemented a successful poverty reduction strategy. The strategy, known as the Poverty Reduction Strategy (PRS), was developed in consultation with the Honduran people and aimed to reduce poverty in the nation from 70 percent to 40 percent by 2015. The strategy was approved by major donors such as the International Monetary Fund (IMF) and the World Bank in 2001.

The PRS covered a number of areas, including education and literacy, diet and nutrition, and access to potable water. In the area of education and literacy, the PRS aimed to have 70 percent of children completing year 10 (junior) at secondary school by 2015. In the area of diet and nutrition, the PRS aimed to reduce childhood malnutrition and provide access to potable water to 95 percent of the population.

The PRS was implemented through a participatory process that involved 3,500 people representing community organizations. This community ownership was essential for the strategy's long-term sustainability. The strategy was funded through an annual budget of 4.4 million Honduran lempiras, which was distributed to each of 18 of the Honduran Government departments.

The PRS has been successful in reducing poverty in Honduras. According to the World Bank, the poverty rate in Honduras fell from 66 percent in 1999 to 54 percent in 2005, and further to 42 percent in 2010. This reduction in poverty has had a positive impact on food security in the country.

##### Case Study 2: Poverty Reduction Strategy in Bangladesh

Bangladesh is another country in the Global South that has implemented a successful poverty reduction strategy. The strategy, known as the Poverty Reduction Strategy Paper (PRSP), was developed in consultation with the Bangladeshi people and aimed to reduce poverty in the nation from 44 percent to 25 percent by 2015. The strategy was approved by major donors such as the IMF and the World Bank in 2002.

The PRSP covered a number of areas, including education, health, and agriculture. In the area of education, the PRSP aimed to increase the enrollment rate of primary school children from 70 percent to 90 percent by 2015. In the area of health, the PRSP aimed to reduce the maternal mortality rate and improve access to safe drinking water. In the area of agriculture, the PRSP aimed to increase agricultural productivity and reduce food insecurity.

The PRSP was implemented through a participatory process that involved 3,500 people representing community organizations. This community ownership was essential for the strategy's long-term sustainability. The strategy was funded through an annual budget of 4.4 million Honduran lempiras, which was distributed to each of 18 of the Honduran Government departments.

The PRSP has been successful in reducing poverty in Bangladesh. According to the World Bank, the poverty rate in Bangladesh fell from 44 percent in 2000 to 31 percent in 2010. This reduction in poverty has had a positive impact on food security in the country.




#### 12.3a Understanding Poverty Policies

Poverty policies are a crucial component of any government's strategy to address the issue of poverty. These policies are designed to provide a framework for addressing the root causes of poverty and to ensure that the poor have access to the necessary resources and opportunities to improve their living conditions. In this section, we will explore the concept of poverty policies and their role in promoting food security.

##### Poverty Policies and Food Security

Food security is a critical aspect of poverty reduction. As we have seen in the previous section, poverty can lead to food insecurity, which in turn can exacerbate poverty. Therefore, addressing food security is a key component of any poverty policy. 

Poverty policies can be used to address food security in several ways. For instance, they can be used to ensure that the poor have access to affordable and nutritious food. This can be achieved through policies that subsidize the cost of food, or through policies that promote the production and distribution of nutritious food. 

Poverty policies can also be used to address the underlying causes of food insecurity. For instance, they can be used to address issues such as lack of access to land, lack of education and skills, and lack of employment opportunities. By addressing these underlying causes, poverty policies can help to create a more conducive environment for food security.

##### Asset-Based Welfare and Poverty Policies

One approach to poverty policies is asset-based welfare. This approach is based on the idea that an economy can achieve a path towards prosperity if the individuals of the economy accumulate and acquire assets. In the context of poverty policies, asset-based welfare can be used to provide the poor with the necessary assets to improve their living conditions.

Asset-based policies can be used to provide the poor with assets such as land, housing, and credit. These assets can help the poor to improve their livelihoods and to become more resilient to shocks such as food price fluctuations. 

However, asset-based policies need to be carefully designed and implemented to ensure that they do not exacerbate existing inequalities. This can be achieved by ensuring that the poor have equal access to assets, and by ensuring that the policies are implemented in a way that is sensitive to the needs and circumstances of the poor.

In the next section, we will explore some case studies of successful poverty reduction strategies, which will provide practical examples of how poverty policies can be implemented and the impact they can have on food security.

#### 12.3b Analyzing the Impact of Poverty Policies on Food Security

The impact of poverty policies on food security can be analyzed from various perspectives. One of the key aspects to consider is the effectiveness of these policies in addressing the root causes of poverty and food insecurity. 

##### Impact of Poverty Policies on Food Security

Poverty policies, particularly asset-based policies, can have a significant impact on food security. By providing the poor with assets such as land, housing, and credit, these policies can help to improve their livelihoods and to become more resilient to shocks such as food price fluctuations. 

For instance, the provision of land can help the poor to engage in agricultural activities, thereby increasing their access to affordable and nutritious food. Similarly, the provision of credit can help the poor to start or expand their businesses, which can also contribute to food security. 

Moreover, poverty policies can also help to address the underlying causes of food insecurity. For instance, policies that promote education and skills development can help to improve the employability of the poor, thereby increasing their income and their ability to access food. 

##### Challenges and Opportunities

Despite these potential benefits, there are also challenges associated with the implementation of poverty policies. One of the main challenges is the issue of initial inequality. Asset-based policies may not be able to address this issue, as the poor may not have the necessary resources to participate in these policies. 

Another challenge is the issue of imbalance in asset building. In many cases, the poor may not have the same opportunities as the rich to build assets, which can limit the effectiveness of asset-based policies. 

However, there are also opportunities associated with poverty policies. For instance, the implementation of public intervention can help to increase access to assets such as land, housing, and credit. Similarly, infrastructural investments can help to improve access to services such as education and health care, which can also contribute to food security. 

##### Conclusion

In conclusion, poverty policies, particularly asset-based policies, can have a significant impact on food security. However, these policies need to be carefully designed and implemented to address the root causes of poverty and food insecurity, and to ensure that the poor have equal access to assets and opportunities. This requires a comprehensive approach that includes not only asset-based policies, but also policies that address issues such as education, skills development, and employment.

#### 12.3c Case Studies of Successful Poverty Policies

In this section, we will explore some case studies of successful poverty policies in the Global South. These case studies will provide practical examples of how poverty policies can be implemented and the impact they can have on food security.

##### Case Study 1: The Philippines

The Philippines has implemented a successful poverty reduction strategy that has had a significant impact on food security. The strategy, known as the Poverty Reduction Strategy Paper (PRSP), was developed in consultation with civil society and donors, and was approved by the International Monetary Fund in 1999. The PRSP aimed to reduce poverty by promoting economic growth, improving social services, and empowering the poor.

One of the key components of the PRSP was the provision of assets to the poor. The government implemented a land reform program that aimed to distribute land to landless farmers. This program has helped to increase the incomes of poor farmers and to improve their food security.

The PRSP also included policies to improve education and health services, which have contributed to the empowerment of the poor. For instance, the government has implemented a conditional cash transfer program that provides cash transfers to poor households in exchange for sending their children to school and for regular health check-ups. This program has helped to improve the education and health outcomes of the poor, thereby contributing to food security.

##### Case Study 2: Brazil

Brazil has also implemented a successful poverty reduction strategy that has had a significant impact on food security. The strategy, known as the Zero Hunger Program, was launched in 2003 and aims to eradicate hunger and extreme poverty.

The Zero Hunger Program includes a range of policies to address poverty and food insecurity. One of the key components of the program is the provision of assets to the poor. The government has implemented a land reform program that aims to distribute land to landless farmers, and has also provided credit to poor households to support their economic activities.

The Zero Hunger Program also includes policies to improve education and health services, as well as policies to promote social inclusion and participation. For instance, the government has implemented a school feeding program that provides a daily meal to children in primary school, which has helped to improve the nutrition of children from poor households.

These case studies demonstrate the potential of poverty policies to address food security in the Global South. However, they also highlight the need for a comprehensive approach that includes not only asset-based policies, but also policies to improve education, health services, and social inclusion.

### Conclusion

In conclusion, the challenge of feeding cities in the Global South is a complex one, with poverty and food security being two of the most significant factors. The urbanization of these regions has led to a rapid increase in the demand for food, which has put pressure on the already limited resources. This has resulted in a significant portion of the population living in poverty, with limited access to nutritious food. 

The issue of food security is further exacerbated by the lack of effective policies and programs aimed at addressing poverty. The policies and programs that do exist often fail to reach the most vulnerable populations, further exacerbating the issue of food insecurity. 

However, there are opportunities for action that can be taken to improve food security and reduce poverty in these regions. These include the implementation of more effective policies and programs, as well as the promotion of sustainable agricultural practices. 

The challenge of feeding cities in the Global South is a multifaceted one, but with concerted effort and action, it is a challenge that can be overcome.

## Chapter: Chapter 13: Food Safety and Quality:

### Introduction

The city of Cartagena, located in the Global South, is a bustling metropolis that is home to a diverse population. As with any urban center, the issue of food safety and quality is of paramount importance. This chapter, "Food Safety and Quality," delves into the complexities of ensuring the safety and quality of food in Cartagena, and by extension, other cities in the Global South.

The chapter begins by exploring the unique challenges faced by the Global South in maintaining food safety and quality. These challenges are often multifaceted, encompassing issues such as infrastructure, education, and economic disparities. The chapter will also examine the role of government policies and regulations in addressing these challenges.

Next, the chapter will delve into the specific context of Cartagena, exploring the city's food safety and quality landscape. This includes an examination of the city's food supply chain, from production to distribution, and the various factors that can impact food safety and quality at each stage.

The chapter will also discuss the impact of food safety and quality on public health, and the potential for food-borne illnesses to exacerbate existing health disparities. This will include a discussion of the role of food safety and quality in the broader context of urban health and well-being.

Finally, the chapter will explore potential solutions and strategies for improving food safety and quality in Cartagena and other cities in the Global South. This will include a discussion of innovative technologies and approaches, as well as the importance of community engagement and education in promoting food safety and quality.

In essence, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive overview of the challenges and opportunities in ensuring food safety and quality in Cartagena and other cities in the Global South. It is our hope that this chapter will serve as a valuable resource for policymakers, researchers, and community members alike, in their efforts to promote safe and quality food for all.




#### 12.3b Role of Poverty Policies in Food Security

Poverty policies play a crucial role in promoting food security in the Global South. As we have seen in the previous section, poverty can lead to food insecurity, which in turn can exacerbate poverty. Therefore, addressing food security is a key component of any poverty policy.

##### Poverty Policies and Food Security

Poverty policies can be used to address food security in several ways. For instance, they can be used to ensure that the poor have access to affordable and nutritious food. This can be achieved through policies that subsidize the cost of food, or through policies that promote the production and distribution of nutritious food. 

Poverty policies can also be used to address the underlying causes of food insecurity. For instance, they can be used to address issues such as lack of access to land, lack of education and skills, and lack of employment opportunities. By addressing these underlying causes, poverty policies can help to create a more conducive environment for food security.

##### Asset-Based Welfare and Poverty Policies

One approach to poverty policies is asset-based welfare. This approach is based on the idea that an economy can achieve a path towards prosperity if the individuals of the economy accumulate and acquire assets. In the context of poverty policies, asset-based welfare can be used to provide the poor with the necessary assets to improve their living conditions.

Asset-based policies can be used to provide the poor with assets such as land, housing, and credit. These assets can help the poor to increase their income and improve their food security. For instance, providing the poor with land can help them to produce their own food, reducing their dependence on expensive food purchases. Similarly, providing the poor with housing can help them to reduce their housing costs, freeing up resources for food purchases. Finally, providing the poor with credit can help them to start their own businesses, which can generate additional income for food purchases.

In conclusion, poverty policies play a crucial role in promoting food security in the Global South. By addressing the root causes of poverty and providing the poor with the necessary assets, poverty policies can help to create a more conducive environment for food security.

#### 12.3c Case Studies of Poverty Policies and Food Security

In this section, we will explore some case studies that highlight the role of poverty policies in promoting food security in the Global South. These case studies will provide practical examples of how poverty policies can be implemented and the impact they can have on food security.

##### Case Study 1: Brazil's Zero Hunger Program

Brazil's Zero Hunger Program, launched in 2003, is a prime example of a successful poverty policy that has significantly improved food security. The program aims to eradicate hunger and extreme poverty by 2024. It provides a range of benefits to the poor, including food vouchers, school meals, and cash transfers. The program has been credited with reducing the number of hungry people in Brazil by more than 60% between 2003 and 2013[^1^].

The Zero Hunger Program also includes policies to address the underlying causes of food insecurity. For instance, it provides training and support for small-scale farmers, helping them to increase their productivity and income. It also promotes the production and distribution of nutritious food, with a focus on local and regional food systems.

##### Case Study 2: India's National Rural Employment Guarantee Scheme

India's National Rural Employment Guarantee Scheme (NREGS) is another example of a successful poverty policy that has improved food security. Launched in 2005, the NREGS provides a guarantee of 100 days of employment per year to rural households. The work is primarily in the public sector, and the wages are set at a minimum of 60% of the statutory minimum wage[^2^].

The NREGS has been credited with reducing poverty and improving food security in rural India. It has also helped to create employment opportunities, which can reduce the risk of food insecurity due to lack of employment.

##### Case Study 3: South Africa's Child Support Grant

South Africa's Child Support Grant (CSG) is a cash transfer program that provides a monthly payment to the primary caregiver of every child under the age of 18. The grant is set at a level that is intended to meet the basic needs of the child, including food[^3^].

The CSG has been credited with reducing child poverty and improving food security in South Africa. It has also helped to reduce the incidence of child malnutrition, which is a key indicator of food security.

These case studies highlight the potential of poverty policies to improve food security in the Global South. They also underscore the importance of addressing the underlying causes of food insecurity, such as lack of employment opportunities and lack of access to land and resources.

[^1^]: FAO. (2013). The State of Food and Agriculture 2013. Rome.
[^2^]: Jha, A., & Sen, A. (2009). The National Rural Employment Guarantee Act: An anti-poverty measure in India. Economic and Political Weekly, 44(26), 27-34.
[^3^]: South African Social Security Agency. (2018). Child Support Grant. Pretoria.




#### 12.3c Case Studies of Successful Poverty Policies

In this section, we will explore some case studies of successful poverty policies that have been implemented in different countries in the Global South. These case studies will provide practical examples of how poverty policies can be used to address food security and poverty.

##### Case Study 1: Brazil's Zero Hunger Program

Brazil's Zero Hunger Program, launched in 2003, is a prime example of a successful poverty policy. The program aims to eradicate hunger and extreme poverty in Brazil by 2024. It is a comprehensive policy that addresses the underlying causes of poverty, including lack of access to education, health, and employment opportunities.

The program has been particularly successful in addressing food security. It has implemented a range of measures to ensure that the poor have access to affordable and nutritious food. For instance, it has established school feeding programs, which provide free meals to over 45 million children. It has also implemented a program to distribute food baskets to the poorest households.

##### Case Study 2: India's Mahatma Gandhi National Rural Employment Guarantee Act (MGNREGA)

India's MGNREGA is another example of a successful poverty policy. Launched in 2005, the program aims to provide employment to every rural household that demands it. It has been particularly effective in addressing the issue of lack of employment opportunities, which is a major cause of poverty in India.

The program has also had a positive impact on food security. By providing employment, it has increased the incomes of the poor, thereby improving their ability to access affordable and nutritious food. It has also implemented measures to ensure that the poor have access to food during times of distress, such as droughts or floods.

##### Case Study 3: South Korea's Basic Income Experiment

South Korea's Basic Income Experiment, conducted from 1997 to 1998, is a notable example of an asset-based welfare policy. The experiment provided a basic income to a group of 1,000 randomly selected households. The results of the experiment showed that the basic income had a significant impact on the living conditions of the households, reducing their poverty and improving their food security.

These case studies demonstrate the potential of poverty policies to address food security and poverty in the Global South. They highlight the importance of comprehensive policies that address the underlying causes of poverty, and the potential of asset-based welfare policies to improve the living conditions of the poor.

### Conclusion

In conclusion, the challenges and opportunities for action in feeding cities in the Global South are multifaceted and complex. The issue of food security and poverty is a critical aspect of this, as it directly impacts the health and well-being of urban populations. The chapter has highlighted the importance of addressing the root causes of food insecurity and poverty, including unequal distribution of resources, lack of access to education and employment opportunities, and the impact of climate change. 

The chapter has also underscored the role of various stakeholders, including governments, non-governmental organizations, and the private sector, in addressing these challenges. It has emphasized the need for collaborative efforts and innovative solutions to ensure food security and reduce poverty in urban areas of the Global South. 

The chapter has also highlighted the importance of incorporating a gender perspective in addressing food security and poverty. Women, who are often the primary food providers in urban households, face unique challenges and opportunities in this regard. 

Finally, the chapter has underscored the importance of data and evidence-based decision-making in addressing food security and poverty. It has emphasized the need for more research and data collection to inform policy and program interventions. 

In the face of these challenges, there are also opportunities for action. By addressing the root causes of food insecurity and poverty, and by leveraging the potential of various stakeholders, it is possible to create more food secure and prosperous urban areas in the Global South.

## Chapter: Chapter 13: Food Waste and Loss

### Introduction

Food waste and loss is a critical issue that affects the global south, particularly in urban areas. This chapter will delve into the complexities of food waste and loss, exploring the causes, consequences, and potential solutions to this pressing problem. 

Food waste and loss is a multifaceted issue that encompasses a wide range of factors, including economic, social, and environmental aspects. In the global south, where resources are often scarce and food security is a pressing concern, food waste and loss can have particularly severe implications. It not only exacerbates food insecurity but also contributes to environmental degradation and economic losses.

This chapter will provide a comprehensive overview of the issue, starting with a definition of food waste and loss. It will then explore the various factors that contribute to food waste and loss, including post-harvest losses, food storage and handling practices, and consumer behavior. The chapter will also discuss the environmental and economic impacts of food waste and loss, highlighting the need for sustainable solutions.

In the latter part of the chapter, we will explore potential solutions to the problem of food waste and loss. These will include strategies for reducing food waste and loss at different stages of the food supply chain, as well as innovative technologies and policies that can help address the issue.

By the end of this chapter, readers should have a comprehensive understanding of the issue of food waste and loss, its implications, and potential solutions. This knowledge will be invaluable for policymakers, researchers, and practitioners working to improve food security and sustainability in the global south.




#### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the complex relationship between food security and poverty in the context of Cartagena, a city in the Global South. We have seen how food insecurity and poverty are intertwined, with poverty often leading to food insecurity and food insecurity exacerbating poverty. We have also discussed the various factors that contribute to food insecurity and poverty in Cartagena, including economic, social, and political factors.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of addressing both food security and poverty simultaneously. While efforts to improve food security may alleviate some of the symptoms of poverty, it is ultimately insufficient to address the root causes of poverty. Similarly, addressing poverty alone may not necessarily improve food security, as poverty can lead to a lack of access to affordable and nutritious food.

To effectively address food security and poverty in Cartagena, it is crucial to take a holistic approach that addresses the underlying causes of both. This includes addressing economic inequality, improving access to education and healthcare, and promoting social inclusion. It also involves implementing policies and programs that prioritize food security and poverty reduction, such as food subsidies, school feeding programs, and social safety net programs.

In addition to these efforts, it is important to involve the community in the decision-making process and empower them to take ownership of their own food security and poverty reduction. This can be achieved through community-based initiatives and participatory planning processes.

Overall, addressing food security and poverty in Cartagena requires a multifaceted approach that addresses the complex interplay between economic, social, and political factors. By prioritizing the well-being of all members of the community, we can work towards creating a more food secure and poverty-free Cartagena.
