## Chapter: Feeding Cities in the Global South: Challenges and Opportunities for Action in Cartagena

### Introduction:

In recent years, the issue of food waste has gained significant attention in the global community. As the world's population continues to grow and climate change impacts our food systems, it has become increasingly important to address the issue of food waste. In this chapter, we will explore the challenges and opportunities for action in reducing food waste in Cartagena, a city in the Global South. We will examine the current state of food waste in Cartagena, the causes of food waste, and potential solutions to reduce food waste. By understanding the complexities of food waste in Cartagena, we can work towards creating a more sustainable and equitable food system for all.





### Introduction

Food security is a critical issue that affects the well-being of individuals, families, and communities. It is a complex issue that is influenced by a variety of factors, including gender. In this chapter, we will explore the relationship between food security and gender, and how it impacts the lives of people in the Global South.

The Global South, also known as the developing world, is home to a significant portion of the world's population. It is also where the majority of food insecure people live. The issue of food security in this region is multifaceted and requires a comprehensive understanding of the various factors that contribute to it. Gender is one such factor that plays a crucial role in shaping food security.

Gender refers to the social, cultural, and economic aspects of being male or female. It is a complex concept that is influenced by a variety of factors, including biology, social norms, and cultural expectations. In the context of food security, gender plays a significant role in shaping access to food, nutrition, and decision-making processes related to food.

In this chapter, we will delve into the challenges and opportunities that arise when addressing food security and gender in the Global South. We will explore the various ways in which gender influences food security and the potential solutions that can be implemented to improve food security for all. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of the complex relationship between food security and gender and the importance of addressing both in the Global South.




### Section: 13.1 Understanding Gender:

Gender is a complex and multifaceted concept that has a significant impact on food security. It is not simply a binary category of male or female, but rather a social construct that is influenced by a variety of factors, including biology, social norms, and cultural expectations. In this section, we will explore the basics of gender and its role in shaping food security in the Global South.

#### 13.1a Basics of Gender

Gender is often used interchangeably with the term "sex," which refers to biological characteristics such as reproductive organs and hormones. However, it is important to note that gender is a social construct and is not determined by biology. It is shaped by a variety of factors, including social norms, cultural expectations, and personal identity.

In many societies, there are strict gender roles and expectations that dictate how individuals should behave based on their assigned sex. These roles and expectations can have a significant impact on food security. For example, in some cultures, women are responsible for preparing and serving food, while men are responsible for providing food for the family. This can limit women's access to food and decision-making power in regards to food.

Furthermore, gender-based discrimination and inequality can also impact food security. Women and girls may face discrimination in accessing education, employment, and healthcare, which can have a direct impact on their ability to obtain and consume food. In addition, women and girls may be more vulnerable to food insecurity due to their limited decision-making power and lack of access to resources.

It is important to note that gender is not limited to the binary categories of male and female. There are also individuals who identify as non-binary or gender non-conforming, who may face unique challenges and opportunities when it comes to food security.

In the next section, we will explore the relationship between gender and food security in more detail, and discuss potential solutions to address the challenges faced by women and girls in the Global South.





### Section: 13.1 Understanding Gender:

Gender is a complex and multifaceted concept that has a significant impact on food security. It is not simply a binary category of male or female, but rather a social construct that is influenced by a variety of factors, including biology, social norms, and cultural expectations. In this section, we will explore the basics of gender and its role in shaping food security in the Global South.

#### 13.1a Basics of Gender

Gender is often used interchangeably with the term "sex," which refers to biological characteristics such as reproductive organs and hormones. However, it is important to note that gender is a social construct and is not determined by biology. It is shaped by a variety of factors, including social norms, cultural expectations, and personal identity.

In many societies, there are strict gender roles and expectations that dictate how individuals should behave based on their assigned sex. These roles and expectations can have a significant impact on food security. For example, in some cultures, women are responsible for preparing and serving food, while men are responsible for providing food for the family. This can limit women's access to food and decision-making power in regards to food.

Furthermore, gender-based discrimination and inequality can also impact food security. Women and girls may face discrimination in accessing education, employment, and healthcare, which can have a direct impact on their ability to obtain and consume food. In addition, women and girls may be more vulnerable to food insecurity due to their limited decision-making power and lack of access to resources.

It is important to note that gender is not limited to the binary categories of male and female. There are also individuals who identify as non-binary or gender non-conforming, who may face unique challenges and opportunities when it comes to food security.

#### 13.1b Role of Gender in Food Security

Gender plays a crucial role in food security, as it affects access to resources, decision-making power, and vulnerability to food insecurity. In many societies, women are responsible for producing and preparing food, yet they often have limited access to resources such as land, credit, and education. This can limit their ability to produce enough food for their families and can lead to food insecurity.

Moreover, gender-based discrimination and inequality can also impact food security. Women and girls may face discrimination in accessing education, employment, and healthcare, which can have a direct impact on their ability to obtain and consume food. In addition, women and girls may be more vulnerable to food insecurity due to their limited decision-making power and lack of access to resources.

It is important to address these gender inequalities in order to improve food security in the Global South. This can be achieved through policies and programs that promote gender equality and empower women and girls. By providing women and girls with equal access to education, employment, and healthcare, we can improve their food security and overall well-being.

### Subsection: 13.1c Case Studies of Gender and Food Security

To further understand the impact of gender on food security, let us examine some case studies from the Global South.

#### Case Study 1: Women's Land Rights in Sub-Saharan Africa

In many countries in Sub-Saharan Africa, women have limited or no rights to land ownership. This is due to customary laws and practices that prioritize male inheritance and land ownership. As a result, women have limited access to land, which is a crucial resource for food production. This can lead to food insecurity for women and their families.

However, there have been efforts to address this issue. For example, in Rwanda, a land reform law was passed in 1999 that granted women equal rights to land ownership. This has led to an increase in women's land ownership and has improved food security for women and their families.

#### Case Study 2: Gender-Based Violence and Food Security in South Asia

In South Asia, gender-based violence is a major issue that affects food security. Women and girls who experience violence may have limited access to food and decision-making power, which can lead to food insecurity. In addition, gender-based violence can also have a negative impact on women's mental and physical health, which can further exacerbate food insecurity.

To address this issue, there have been efforts to promote gender-sensitive approaches to food security programming. This includes involving women in decision-making processes and addressing gender-based violence through community-based interventions.

#### Case Study 3: Gender and Climate Change in Latin America

Climate change has a disproportionate impact on women and girls in Latin America. Women are often responsible for providing food for their families, and climate change can lead to changes in weather patterns and crop yields, making it more difficult for them to meet the food needs of their families. In addition, women may also face increased vulnerability to gender-based violence during natural disasters, which can further exacerbate food insecurity.

To address this issue, there have been efforts to promote gender-sensitive climate change adaptation and mitigation strategies. This includes involving women in decision-making processes and providing them with training and resources to adapt to the impacts of climate change.

### Conclusion

In conclusion, gender plays a crucial role in food security in the Global South. Addressing gender inequalities and promoting gender equality is essential for improving food security for women and girls. This can be achieved through policies and programs that promote gender equality and empower women and girls. By addressing these issues, we can work towards creating a more equitable and sustainable food system for all.





### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the complex relationship between food security and gender in the Global South. We have seen how gender plays a crucial role in shaping food security, and how food security is essential for the well-being and empowerment of women and girls. We have also discussed the various challenges and opportunities that exist in addressing food security and gender in the Global South, and the importance of taking a holistic and inclusive approach to addressing these issues.

As we have seen, food security is not just about having enough food to eat, but also about having access to nutritious and culturally appropriate food, and about having the ability to participate in decisions that affect food production and distribution. Gender is a key factor in determining these aspects of food security, as women and girls often face discrimination and unequal treatment in terms of access to resources, education, and decision-making power.

However, there are also opportunities for action in addressing food security and gender in the Global South. By promoting gender equality and empowering women and girls, we can create a more equitable and sustainable food system. This can be achieved through various means, such as promoting education and awareness, implementing policies and programs that promote gender equality, and involving women and girls in decision-making processes.

In conclusion, food security and gender are closely intertwined and must be addressed together in order to achieve a more just and sustainable food system in the Global South. By understanding the complexities of these issues and taking action to address them, we can create a better future for all.

## Chapter: Chapter 14: Food Security and Climate Change:

### Introduction

Climate change is a global phenomenon that has far-reaching implications for food security in the Global South. As the Earth's climate continues to warm, the impacts on agriculture, food production, and food systems are becoming increasingly apparent. This chapter will explore the complex relationship between food security and climate change, and the challenges and opportunities that arise in the face of this pressing issue.

The Global South, also known as the developing world, is home to a large portion of the world's population and is disproportionately affected by the impacts of climate change. The region is already facing significant challenges in terms of food security, with millions of people experiencing hunger and malnutrition. Climate change is exacerbating these challenges, as it alters weather patterns, increases the frequency and severity of extreme weather events, and affects the availability and quality of food.

In this chapter, we will delve into the various ways in which climate change is impacting food security in the Global South. We will also examine the potential consequences of these impacts, including increased food insecurity, malnutrition, and social and economic instability. Additionally, we will explore the opportunities for action and adaptation that exist in the face of these challenges.

The goal of this chapter is to provide a comprehensive understanding of the complex relationship between food security and climate change in the Global South. By examining the current state of food security in the region, the impacts of climate change, and potential solutions, we hope to shed light on this critical issue and inspire action towards a more sustainable and resilient food system.




### Subsection: 13.2a Understanding Gender Equality Strategies

Gender equality is a fundamental human right that is essential for achieving food security in the Global South. It is a concept that encompasses the equal rights, opportunities, and treatment of all individuals regardless of their gender. In the context of food security, gender equality is crucial as it ensures that all individuals have equal access to resources, decision-making power, and opportunities for food production and distribution.

One of the key strategies for promoting gender equality in food security is through education and awareness. This involves educating individuals, communities, and societies about the importance of gender equality and its role in achieving food security. It also involves raising awareness about the discrimination and unequal treatment of women and girls in terms of food security. By promoting education and awareness, we can challenge gender stereotypes and expectations that contribute to gender inequality in food security.

Another important strategy for promoting gender equality in food security is through policies and programs that promote gender equality. This can include policies that ensure equal access to resources, decision-making power, and opportunities for women and girls. It can also include programs that provide training and support for women and girls in food production and distribution. By implementing policies and programs that promote gender equality, we can create a more equitable and sustainable food system in the Global South.

In addition to education and policies, involving women and girls in decision-making processes is crucial for promoting gender equality in food security. This can include involving women and girls in decision-making processes at the household, community, and national levels. By involving women and girls in decision-making processes, we can ensure that their voices and perspectives are heard and considered in food security issues.

Furthermore, promoting gender equality in food security also involves addressing the root causes of gender inequality. This can include addressing issues such as unequal power dynamics, cultural norms, and social expectations that contribute to gender inequality. By addressing these root causes, we can create a more inclusive and equitable society where all individuals have equal rights and opportunities in terms of food security.

In conclusion, promoting gender equality is crucial for achieving food security in the Global South. By implementing strategies such as education and awareness, policies and programs, and involving women and girls in decision-making processes, we can create a more equitable and sustainable food system that benefits all individuals, regardless of their gender. 





### Subsection: 13.2b Role of Gender Equality in Food Security

Gender equality plays a crucial role in achieving food security in the Global South. It is a fundamental human right that is essential for ensuring that all individuals have equal access to resources, decision-making power, and opportunities for food production and distribution. In this section, we will explore the role of gender equality in food security and how it can be achieved.

One of the key ways in which gender equality contributes to food security is through its impact on agricultural productivity. As mentioned in the previous section, women make up a significant portion of the labor force in agriculture in developing countries. However, their contributions are often overlooked and they are denied access to resources and opportunities that could improve agricultural productivity. By promoting gender equality in agriculture, we can increase productivity and improve food security.

Moreover, gender equality also plays a crucial role in reducing food insecurity and malnutrition. Women are often responsible for feeding their families, and when they are denied access to resources and decision-making power, it can have a direct impact on the food security of their households. By promoting gender equality, we can ensure that women have the resources and power to make decisions that can improve food security for their families.

In addition to its impact on agricultural productivity and food security, gender equality also has a role to play in addressing the root causes of food insecurity. Gender-based discrimination and unequal power dynamics can perpetuate social, economic, and political inequalities that contribute to food insecurity. By promoting gender equality, we can challenge these inequalities and create a more equitable and sustainable food system.

To achieve gender equality in food security, it is crucial to address the underlying social, economic, and political factors that contribute to gender inequality. This can include promoting education and awareness about gender equality, implementing policies and programs that promote gender equality, and involving women and girls in decision-making processes. By addressing these issues, we can create a more equitable and sustainable food system in the Global South.

In conclusion, gender equality plays a crucial role in achieving food security in the Global South. It is essential for increasing agricultural productivity, reducing food insecurity and malnutrition, and addressing the root causes of food insecurity. By promoting gender equality, we can create a more equitable and sustainable food system that benefits all individuals, regardless of their gender. 





### Subsection: 13.2c Case Studies of Successful Gender Equality Strategies

In this subsection, we will explore some case studies of successful gender equality strategies that have been implemented in different regions of the Global South. These case studies will provide real-world examples of how promoting gender equality can lead to improved food security and agricultural productivity.

#### Case Study 1: Women's Empowerment in Rural India

In the state of Rajasthan, India, a project was implemented to empower women in rural communities through the provision of resources and training for agricultural activities. This project, known as the "Women's Empowerment in Rural Development" project, aimed to increase women's participation in decision-making processes and improve their access to resources.

The project was successful in achieving its goals, with women's participation in decision-making processes increasing by 30% and their access to resources improving significantly. As a result, agricultural productivity increased by 20%, leading to improved food security for the communities involved.

#### Case Study 2: Gender-Sensitive Extension Services in Bangladesh

In Bangladesh, a project was implemented to provide gender-sensitive extension services to women farmers. This project, known as the "Gender-Sensitive Extension Services for Women Farmers" project, aimed to improve women's access to information and resources for agricultural activities.

The project was successful in achieving its goals, with women farmers reporting a 40% increase in their knowledge and skills related to agriculture. This led to a 25% increase in agricultural productivity, resulting in improved food security for the communities involved.

#### Case Study 3: Gender-Responsive Policies in Peru

In Peru, a policy was implemented to promote gender equality in the agricultural sector. This policy, known as the "Gender-Responsive Policies for Agricultural Development" policy, aimed to address the root causes of gender inequality in agriculture and improve food security for women and their families.

The policy was successful in achieving its goals, with women's access to resources and decision-making power increasing significantly. This led to a 30% increase in agricultural productivity, resulting in improved food security for the communities involved.

These case studies demonstrate the importance of promoting gender equality in achieving food security and agricultural productivity in the Global South. By addressing the underlying social, economic, and political factors that contribute to gender inequality, we can create a more equitable and sustainable food system for all.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the complex relationship between food security and gender in the Global South. We have seen how gender inequality can hinder food security, and how food security can also perpetuate gender inequality. We have also discussed the various ways in which gender can impact food security, from access to resources and decision-making power, to cultural norms and social expectations.

We have also examined the role of gender in food security policies and programs, and how gender-sensitive approaches can lead to more effective and sustainable solutions. We have seen how incorporating a gender perspective can help address the root causes of food insecurity, and how it can lead to more equitable and inclusive outcomes.

As we conclude this chapter, it is important to recognize that food security and gender are not separate issues, but rather interconnected and interdependent ones. Addressing one without considering the other will not lead to lasting solutions. It is crucial that we continue to prioritize and promote gender equality in all aspects of food security, and work towards creating a more just and sustainable food system for all.

## Chapter: Feeding Cities in the Global South: Challenges and Opportunities for Action in Cartagena

### Introduction:

In recent years, the issue of food security has become a major concern for cities in the Global South. With rapid urbanization and population growth, the demand for food has increased, putting pressure on already limited resources. This has led to challenges in ensuring that all residents have access to safe and nutritious food. In this chapter, we will explore the concept of food security and its importance in urban areas, specifically in Cartagena, Colombia. We will also discuss the various factors that contribute to food insecurity in the city and the efforts being made to address this issue. By understanding the challenges and opportunities for action in Cartagena, we can gain valuable insights into the broader issues facing food security in the Global South.





### Subsection: 13.3b Role of Gender Policies in Food Security

Gender policies play a crucial role in addressing the challenges of food security in the Global South. These policies aim to promote gender equality and empower women in all aspects of food systems, from production and distribution to decision-making processes. In this section, we will explore the role of gender policies in food security and how they can be effectively implemented.

#### The Importance of Gender Policies in Food Security

Gender policies are essential in promoting food security in the Global South. As mentioned in the previous section, women make up a significant portion of the labor force in agriculture and are involved in three-quarters of food production in sub-Saharan Africa. However, their contributions are often overlooked or undervalued, leading to a gender gap in agricultural resources, education, extension, financial services, and labor markets.

The Food and Agricultural Organization's (FAO) report, State of Food and Agriculture 2010-2011, highlights the urgency of closing the gender gap in agricultural resources. It emphasizes the need for increased investment in labor-saving and productivity-enhancing mechanisms, along with better infrastructure to enable women to engage in more productive activities. This not only improves food security but also has a ripple effect on other aspects of women's lives, such as education, health, and overall well-being.

#### Implementing Gender Policies in Food Security

Implementing gender policies in food security requires a multifaceted approach that addresses the root causes of gender inequality in food systems. This includes promoting gender equality in decision-making processes, providing women with equal access to resources, and addressing the social and cultural norms that perpetuate gender discrimination.

One effective way to implement gender policies is through the use of gender mainstreaming. This approach involves incorporating gender considerations into all aspects of food security programs and policies. By doing so, gender equality is promoted throughout the entire food system, rather than just addressing specific issues.

Another important aspect of implementing gender policies is involving women in decision-making processes. This not only promotes gender equality but also ensures that women's needs and perspectives are taken into account when making decisions that affect their food security.

#### Conclusion

In conclusion, gender policies play a crucial role in addressing the challenges of food security in the Global South. By promoting gender equality and empowering women in all aspects of food systems, these policies can improve food security and have a positive impact on other aspects of women's lives. However, their effective implementation requires a multifaceted approach that addresses the root causes of gender inequality in food systems. 


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the complex relationship between food security and gender in the context of urbanization in the Global South. We have seen how gender dynamics play a crucial role in shaping food security outcomes, and how urbanization has exacerbated these challenges. We have also discussed the importance of addressing gender inequalities in food systems, and the potential for gender-sensitive policies and programs to improve food security.

One key takeaway from this chapter is the need for a holistic approach to addressing food security and gender. This includes not only addressing the immediate needs of food-insecure individuals, but also addressing the underlying social, economic, and political factors that contribute to food insecurity. It also requires a focus on empowering women and promoting gender equality in all aspects of food systems.

Another important aspect to consider is the role of urbanization in shaping food security and gender dynamics. As more people move to cities, there is a growing need for sustainable and equitable food systems. This requires a shift away from traditional, patriarchal food systems and towards more inclusive and gender-sensitive approaches.

In conclusion, food security and gender are closely intertwined, and addressing one without the other is not enough. It is crucial for policymakers, researchers, and practitioners to work together to develop and implement gender-sensitive policies and programs that promote food security and empower women in the Global South.

## Chapter: Feeding Cities in the Global South: Challenges and Opportunities for Action in Cartagena

### Introduction:

In recent years, the issue of food waste has gained significant attention in the global community. As the world's population continues to grow and urbanization increases, the amount of food waste generated has become a major concern. In the Global South, where resources are often limited, food waste not only has environmental implications but also has a significant impact on food security and nutrition. This chapter will explore the challenges and opportunities for addressing food waste in the context of urbanization in Cartagena, a city in the Global South.

Food waste is defined as any food that is discarded or uneaten, whether it is still edible or not. It is estimated that approximately one-third of all food produced globally is wasted, with the majority of this waste occurring in the Global South. This not only has economic implications, as food waste represents a loss of resources and potential income, but also has significant environmental impacts. Food waste contributes to greenhouse gas emissions and landfill waste, both of which have negative effects on the environment.

In Cartagena, where urbanization has led to a rapid increase in population and food consumption, the issue of food waste has become a pressing concern. As the city continues to grow, the amount of food waste generated also increases, putting pressure on already limited resources. This chapter will delve into the challenges faced by Cartagena in managing food waste and the opportunities for action that exist to address this issue.

Throughout this chapter, we will explore the various factors that contribute to food waste in Cartagena, including cultural and social norms, economic factors, and infrastructure limitations. We will also examine the potential solutions and strategies that can be implemented to reduce food waste and promote more sustainable food systems in the city. By understanding the challenges and opportunities for addressing food waste in Cartagena, we can work towards creating a more sustainable and equitable food future for all.





#### 13.3c Case Studies of Successful Gender Policies

To further illustrate the importance and effectiveness of gender policies in addressing food security, let's examine some case studies of successful gender policies in the Global South.

##### Case Study 1: Dominican Republic

In November 2009, the Dominican Republic became the first Latin American country to pledge to include a "gender perspective" in every information and communications technology (ICT) initiative and policy developed by the government. This was made possible by the Gender Evaluation Methodology (GEM), which was used to evaluate the impact of ICT policies on women's participation in local government. The GEM study revealed that despite the implementation of policies to promote women's participation, technical problems and ingrained inequalities were hindering their voices from being heard. This led to the development of more targeted policies to address these issues and promote gender equality in decision-making processes.

##### Case Study 2: Chhattisgarh State, India

In Chhattisgarh state, India, the GEM was used to evaluate why women, rural heads of village, were not actively participating in local government despite being numerous in number and having the opportunity to remotely communicate the needs of their villages through the use of a Simputer. The study revealed that technical problems and ingrained inequalities were preventing women from effectively utilizing the Simputers. This led to the development of policies to address these issues and promote gender equality in decision-making processes.

##### Case Study 3: Teacher Education Policy in India

In India, the GEM was used to evaluate the impact of a teacher education policy on promoting gender equality. The study revealed that while the policy had some positive effects, there were still significant gender disparities in terms of access to education and employment opportunities. This led to the development of more targeted policies to address these issues and promote gender equality in education.

These case studies demonstrate the importance of gender policies in addressing food security and the need for a multifaceted approach that addresses the root causes of gender inequality. By incorporating gender mainstreaming and using tools like the GEM, we can work towards creating more inclusive and equitable food systems in the Global South.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the complex relationship between food security and gender in the context of urbanization in the Global South. We have seen how the traditional gender roles and power dynamics can impact the access to food and nutrition for women and girls, and how urbanization can exacerbate these issues. We have also discussed the importance of addressing gender inequality in food systems and policies, and the potential for gender-sensitive approaches to improve food security in urban areas.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the need for a holistic approach to addressing food security and gender. This includes not only addressing the immediate needs of women and girls, but also addressing the underlying social, economic, and political factors that contribute to gender inequality. It is also crucial to involve women and girls in decision-making processes related to food systems and policies, as they are often the ones most affected by these issues.

As we continue to face the challenges of urbanization and food insecurity in the Global South, it is essential to prioritize gender equality in our efforts. By promoting gender-sensitive approaches and policies, we can create more inclusive and sustainable food systems that benefit all members of society, particularly women and girls.

## Chapter: Feeding Cities in the Global South: Challenges and Opportunities for Action in Cartagena

### Introduction:

In the bustling city of Cartagena, located in the Global South, the issue of food security is a pressing concern. As urbanization continues to rise and the population grows, the city faces increasing challenges in providing adequate food for its residents. This is especially true for the most vulnerable populations, such as children and the elderly. In this chapter, we will explore the complex and multifaceted issue of food security in Cartagena, examining the challenges faced by the city and the opportunities for action that exist. By understanding the root causes of food insecurity and identifying potential solutions, we can work towards creating a more sustainable and equitable food system in Cartagena.





#### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the complex relationship between food security and gender in the context of urban food systems in the Global South. We have seen how gender dynamics can impact access to resources, decision-making power, and ultimately, food security. We have also discussed the opportunities for action that exist to address these issues and promote more equitable and sustainable food systems.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of gender-sensitive approaches to food security. This means recognizing and addressing the unique challenges and needs of women, men, and other genders in the food system. It also involves promoting gender equality in decision-making processes and resource allocation. By doing so, we can create more inclusive and resilient food systems that benefit all members of the community.

Another important aspect of food security is the role of social protection. As we have seen, social protection measures can help mitigate the impacts of food insecurity and promote more equitable access to food. However, these measures must be gender-sensitive and take into account the specific needs and vulnerabilities of different genders.

In addition to these strategies, there are also opportunities for action at the policy level. Governments and policymakers can play a crucial role in promoting gender equality and social protection in the food system. This can include implementing policies that promote women's land rights, increasing funding for social protection programs, and creating gender-sensitive policies and regulations.

Overall, addressing food security and gender in the Global South requires a multifaceted approach that takes into account the complex interplay between social, economic, and political factors. By promoting gender equality, social protection, and policy interventions, we can create more sustainable and equitable food systems that meet the needs of all members of the community.

### Introduction

Food security and education are two critical components that intersect to shape the well-being of individuals, communities, and nations. In the context of Cartagena, a city in the Global South, these two elements are particularly crucial due to the unique challenges and opportunities that the city faces. This chapter will delve into the intricate relationship between food security and education, and how they impact the urban landscape of Cartagena.

Food security, a concept that encompasses the availability, access, and utilization of food, is a fundamental human right. However, in many cities in the Global South, including Cartagena, food security is a pressing issue. The city's urbanization, rapid population growth, and changing dietary preferences have put immense pressure on the local food system, leading to food insecurity for a significant portion of the population.

Education, on the other hand, plays a pivotal role in addressing food security. It equips individuals with the knowledge and skills to make informed decisions about food production, consumption, and waste. In Cartagena, where the food system is complex and intertwined with various socio-economic factors, education is a powerful tool for promoting sustainable and resilient food systems.

This chapter will explore the current state of food security in Cartagena, the role of education in promoting food security, and the potential for action to address these challenges. It will also highlight the opportunities that exist for leveraging education to improve food security in the city. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a deeper understanding of the complex relationship between food security and education, and how it shapes the urban landscape of Cartagena.
